<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_21b60a9a-9b7d-426a-89d9-e29018a68cdd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer7033445455045353612">When a beautiful aspiring writer strides into the East Village bookstore where Joe Goldberg works, he does what anyone would do: he Googles the name on her credit card.<br/><br/>There is only one Guinevere Beck in New York City. She has a public Facebook account and Tweets incessantly, telling Joe everything he needs to know: she is simply Beck to her friends, she went to Brown Univ</span>
  <span id="freeText7033445455045353612" style="display:none">When a beautiful aspiring writer strides into the East Village bookstore where Joe Goldberg works, he does what anyone would do: he Googles the name on her credit card.<br /><br />There is only one Guinevere Beck in New York City. She has a public Facebook account and Tweets incessantly, telling Joe everything he needs to know: she is simply Beck to her friends, she went to Brown University, she lives on Bank Street, and she’ll be at a bar in Brooklyn tonight—the perfect place for a “chance” meeting.<br /><br />As Joe invisibly and obsessively takes control of Beck’s life, he orchestrates a series of events to ensure Beck finds herself in his waiting arms. Moving from stalker to boyfriend, Joe transforms himself into Beck’s perfect man, all while quietly removing the obstacles that stand in their way—even if it means murder.<br /><br />A terrifying exploration of how vulnerable we all are to stalking and manipulation, debut author Caroline Kepnes delivers a razor-sharp novel for our hyper-connected digital age.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7033445455045353612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476785592" href="/book/show/20821614-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1082804588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8069418758321588135"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413775343i/11561439._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>I'm not sure what crazy people shelved this book as "romance". <i>You</i> is romantic in the same way that <i>Lolita</i> is romantic. In other words: an <b>insane, obsessive and manipulative</b> romance from the perspective of a charming psychopath.<br/><br/>It's a fucked up tale told from the POV of a stalker who obsesses over and spies on a young woman. He gradually plants himself into her life and seeks a relationship with her, whilst simultaneously hacking her emails and following every little thing she does. If you're lo</span>
  <span id="freeText8069418758321588135" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413775343i/11561439._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I'm not sure what crazy people shelved this book as "romance". <i>You</i> is romantic in the same way that <i>Lolita</i> is romantic. In other words: an <b>insane, obsessive and manipulative</b> romance from the perspective of a charming psychopath.<br><br>It's a fucked up tale told from the POV of a stalker who obsesses over and spies on a young woman. He gradually plants himself into her life and seeks a relationship with her, whilst simultaneously hacking her emails and following every little thing she does. If you're looking for a creeptastic story just in time for Halloween then you need look no further.<br><br>What is perhaps most unsettling about our narrator is how closely he resembles some of the love interests in YA and NA romance books. Telling his unreliable tale, Joe truly believes that he and Beck are meant to be. His narration is completely insane, horrifying and - at times - beautiful.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413777005i/11561664._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>He is a fantastically unreliable narrator, made more so by the charm and humour he uses to engage the reader. Like Humbert from <i>Lolita</i>, Joe's intelligence, wit and candor make it easy to sympathize with him, even though we are aware of how twisted he really is. <br><br>The novel evades the boundaries of genre; not quite a contemporary, maybe, but also unlike most psychological thrillers, creating something new and complex - quite unlike anything I've ever read before. Being inside Joe's head is a poisonous but admittedly fascinating place to be. Through him, the author examines the games people play with one another and the gentle manipulation that even the most innocent of us are capable of at times:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413777463i/11561719._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>You</i> also offers an interesting look at stalking in the digital age. Joe is able to commit his crimes through the use of email, Facebook and Twitter; finding out huge amounts of information about Beck without even leaving his house. It made me incredibly aware of how visible we all are these days and had me almost looking over my own shoulder as I was reading it.<br><br><b>A random spur of the moment read that really paid off.</b><br><br><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8069418758321588135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12096503272112577736" style="display:none">I finished this book while recovering from surgery. I was medicated and kind of loopy. Considering how weird this book is, it is kind of perfect!<br /><br />Not for the faint of heart! This book is demented and twisted. You will feel uncomfortable that the words on these pages came from someone and were actually published. You will feel guilty for being enthralled by the madness and behavior of the narrator. You will start to question your own sanity as you realize you are not quite sure who you are cheering for.<br /><br />For lovers of twisted horror that touches on the potential insanity of the human psyche, this book is for you! If you read my review, and then you read the book and you are grossed out, disturbed, or upset by the content, don't blame me! You can only blame YOU!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1994693500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1994693500" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1994693500?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476785608" href="/book/show/23492630-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=what-is-this-mess">what-is-this-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2018">z-read2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-audiobook">x-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=genre-experiments">genre-experiments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1994693500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2601430580270497200">UPDATE: I am officially muting comments on this review because they without fail make me hate my life. You can take my points or you can leave them. It's a book review. If your point is "thinking critically about media is stupid and bad", I can absolutely promise you I do not care. If you want to see my personal hell you can read through the comments on this. <br/><br/>************<br/><br/><i>You</i> is a book I should hypothetically like because it is messed up and creepy. But unfortunately it’s also – and don’t kill me</span>
  <span id="freeText2601430580270497200" style="display:none">UPDATE: I am officially muting comments on this review because they without fail make me hate my life. You can take my points or you can leave them. It's a book review. If your point is "thinking critically about media is stupid and bad", I can absolutely promise you I do not care. If you want to see my personal hell you can read through the comments on this. <br /><br />************<br /><br /><i>You</i> is a book I should hypothetically like because it is messed up and creepy. But unfortunately it’s also – and don’t kill me, I’m going to explain why I feel this way – <b>not very good</b>. <br /><br />This is a book about a stalker, with one interesting twist: he narrates. Which is horrifying and... kind of interesting, and Santino Fontana deserves an award for his audiobook narration. I will fully admit that this book does one thing really well: it makes you feel as if it could happen to <i>you</i>, to anyone. <b>There’s something really scary about a thriller in which the villain is so outwardly nice, even believing within his mind that he IS kind.</b> You can completely see why someone like Beck (who never goes beyond the outline of a person) likes Joe. <br /><br />The issue is that the ENTIRE BOOK is based off this gimmick, and it is four hundred twenty pages, and very little is done with the premise. I feel the need to explain <b>how minimal the plot is:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[this book felt, to me, like it was building up to a revelation in which the girl Joe is stalking is actually going to try and kill him, which would’ve been so fucking badass. and then... He kills her and meets a new victim and that’s basically... it <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <b>It's just... um, can't you can get the entire plot of this book from the blurb?</b><br /><br />My other problem with this book is that the narrative uses a purposeful failure to develop side characters to manipulate the audience. The narrative gains empathy for Joe by <b>making you feel like you <i>should</i> feel empathy for Joe</b>, and does it via what I think is a very boring path: i.e. by villainizing all the side characters and forgoing character depth entirely. <br /><br />Benjy and Peach are both awful and annoying and I don’t have any sympathy for either one of these characters. But… that’s because Caroline Kepnes doesn’t want me to. These two characters are villainized, with every moment of depth to their character taken away, so the narrative can find Joe— remember, the stalker, the dude who watches a girl masturbate and kidnaps and murders her?— the more sympathetic character. <br /><br />See, Kepnes sometimes does this thing with Beck where Beck will do something, Joe will think a thing about her motivations, and the audience can see on some level that he’s wrong, but... we wonder. THAT is a solid unreliable narrator—the lack of ability to figure out what’s real and what’s fake. But that delightful ambiguity is <i>missing</i> from most of the narrative. There is something so lazy and frustrating about caricaturizing the people around a stalker so you can gain audience sympathy for said stalker. <br /><br />Peach, specifically, is an example of both <a href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/PsychoLesbian" rel="nofollow noopener">the predatory lesbian trope</a> and also <a href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/BuryYourGays" rel="nofollow noopener">the bury your gays trope</a>. Peach, on-page, masturbates to naked photos of her best friend that her best friend does not know she has. This is messed up behavior. Though of course he exaggerates this, Joe is <i>proven right</i> that Peach is, on some level, dangerous, and the audience feels no grief at her death. Love the only gay character in the book being a borderline sexual predator. It's not at all done before and absolutely was not mandated by law in the us to show how horrible and creepy gay people were. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_homosexuality_in_American_film#World_War_II_era_to_1960s" rel="nofollow noopener">Oh no, really</a>.<br /><br />I also found the running joke about chronic illnesses sort of strange. Joe keeps believing that everyone he knows is faking both their food allergies and chronic illnesses and in at least one circumstance, he’s proven right (Peach, again), thus proving <b>“everyone in New York is faking illnesses”</b> as <i>right</i>. Joe also does incredibly relatable customer service rants and both things are written in the same tone, set up in connection to Joe's annoyance with political correctness and elitism. Comments about People With Chronic Illnesses are framed in the same light as jokes about annoying Brooklyn hipsters, and I question the point of this. <br /><br />I get that to some readers, morality codes don’t apply because this book is ~edgy~ and ~dark~. And I enjoy compelling moral darkness. I just also know that implying people make up food allergies for fun isn’t compelling moral darkness, and playing into old tropes about lesbians isn't compelling moral darkness either. Playing into social norms isn't actually edgy at all, it's just kind of... boring. As the book continues, I almost found myself... bored. A derisive rant about Brooklyn hipsters is fun for a while, but not for 60% of a thriller. <br /><br /><b>Glad you want to be edgy. Wish you could do it in a way that actually transgresses societal norms rather than enforcing them.</b> I would love to think this book is being 'meta', sure, but I don't see a reason to think it is. And frankly, I wouldn't have liked it anyway. <br /><br />EDIT #1: Based on the incredible amount of angry comments on this review, I think it's very important that we, as a society, google the Hays Code, or watch the Celluloid Closet, or even, very quickly, attempt to read the wikipedia article about <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_homosexuality_in_American_film#World_War_II_era_to_1960s" rel="nofollow noopener">the history of representation of gay, bi, and trans people in cinema</a>. No, actually, it is not ever necessary to add a predatory lesbian who dies at the end to your book that contains no gay people. No, it is not subversive, and no, it is not new. It is important, in media literacy, to consider the impacts of the portrayals of gay and bi women. Please think critically. <br /><br />Overall: <b>
  <u>I’m just not impressed.</u>
</b> yes, Kepnes can write, and yes, the concept is excellent. but there's nothing being done here. I’m annoyed that with such an interesting premise and with such wonderful writing, this felt so lazy. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2601430580270497200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2706840926" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2706840926" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2706840926?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2706840926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9652884899723946456"><b>4.2</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br/><br/><blockquote>“The problem with books is that they end.” </blockquote><br/><br/>Well, well, well. This is me reading the book after I have watched the TV adaptation. "adding gif of shame scene from Game of Thrones". Oh, well. <b>Hang me.</b> But let's talk about the book now. This is an extremely addicting, gripping and engaging book. Don't let the fact that it took me 9 days to finish this book mislead you from how obsessed I was with it, life is just like that. I could finish this book in a day, if I could. This i</span>
  <span id="freeText9652884899723946456" style="display:none"><b>4.2</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br /><br /><blockquote>“The problem with books is that they end.” </blockquote><br /><br />Well, well, well. This is me reading the book after I have watched the TV adaptation. "adding gif of shame scene from Game of Thrones". Oh, well. <b>Hang me.</b> But let's talk about the book now. This is an extremely addicting, gripping and engaging book. Don't let the fact that it took me 9 days to finish this book mislead you from how obsessed I was with it, life is just like that. I could finish this book in a day, if I could. This is how fucking catchy it is, like a fucking cold you can't shake off. And that reminds me, it's flu season. <b>Yikes.</b><br /><br /><i>There is only one Guinevere Beck in New York City. She has a public Facebook account and Tweets incessantly, telling Joe everything he needs to know: she is simply Beck to her friends, she went to Brown University, she lives on Bank Street, and she’ll be at a bar in Brooklyn tonight—the perfect place for a “chance” meeting.<br /><br />As Joe invisibly and obsessively takes control of Beck’s life, he orchestrates a series of events to ensure Beck finds herself in his waiting arms. Moving from stalker to boyfriend, Joe transforms himself into Beck’s perfect man, all while quietly removing the obstacles that stand in their way—even if it means murder.</i><br /><br />This book is not for everyone. It's violent, it's sexual, it's manipulative, it's appalling, it might be too much for you. But if you're a person like me, who can fucking watch anything and everything and won't be bothered by fucking nothing. then you have found your book. The fact that Joe is talking in second person, to Beck, is making this book a lot more creepy and stalky. Hence the way I'm gonna be talking in this review.<br /><br />What amazes me in this book is how fucking normal Joe seems to appear to the world. If we saw the story from Beck's POV, we would fall in love with him as she did. He's a good looking guy who works in a bookstore (yummy), he's funny, he's charismatic, he knows his shit. And beyond everything else... a creepy stalking psychotic killer. This character reminds me of Ted Bundy and now I'm fucking scared. Joe is a character who you want to hate but you can't, at some points. You just feel sorry for him and it's fucking frustrating and wrong. So wrong. But you can't shake this feeling. And that's how good the author portrayed the character. <br /><br />When it comes to Beck, the rose of Joe's life, I ain't buying it. <b>The bitch pissed me off.</b> She treats people like garbage, she's shallow, egotistical, selfish, and she's never short of an excuse about the shitty and irresponsible shit she's pulling. I can't understand what Joe saw in her. Maybe he saw his flawed self in her. Everyone who is obsessed with Beck, seem to be people with issues. <br /><br />I want to talk about the TV show now, and the differences from the book. There are obviously characters and storylines that were included in the TV show that didn't exist in the book and vice versa. But I believe, what the show lacked the book provided and backwards. The whole storyline with Paco and his malfunctioning family didn't exist in the book, and I believe this was a weakness of the book. This character, this little kid really showed us that Joe had a good side beside all his issues. That he wanted to help someone, without having to get something out of it. It was sweet. Also, Candace is dead in the book. Which makes me wonder, what the fuck is left to happen in the next book? I guess I'll find out when I eventually read it. Furthermore, Beck never saw Joe at the Dicken's festival and he never met her family. Which was a scene that I wanted in the book, to be honest. In addition, in the book they didn't have a relationship right away. In the TV show, they started dating right after the dreaded <b>"8 seconds"</b> (LMFAO). In the book, it took lots of time for the blinding fucking to commence. This is television, I guess. There were some other differences that I don't think are worth mentioning. I think the show was quicker and had more storylines just because it's TV, whereas the book was a tad bit slower. Which didn't bother me in the least. <br /><br />The last 100 pages man. My heartbeat was at God limits. Those last 100 pages, showed exactly how sick and delusional Joe is. He honestly thought Beck was in the wrong just because "she snooped at his stuff". He thought she would wanna be with him because this is how a man shows his love. He wanted to showcase his killings, his bordeline obsession, his unrelenting stalking. His thoughts throughout those last few pages frightened me to death. The author did a marvelous job in the horror aspect. <br /><br />Overall, I truly enjoyed this book. It was obsessive, steamy, funny, sick and motherfucking incredible. I would recommend it to people who can handle shit being thrown raw at them, so be cautious before starting it. When I got time, I plan on rewatching the show... or maybe I'll do it when season 2 comes out. Don't know, will decide. But I definitely plan on visiting the next book, even though I have no idea what the fuck is left to happen. Anyways! Till the next one K BYE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9652884899723946456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1836102603" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1836102603" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1836102603?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476785592" href="/book/show/20821614-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1836102603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9684533666417810562">Wow, this read was a trip! It’s been a hot minute since I’ve read something so psychologically twisted but I am ever so pleased.<br/><br/>CW: violence, murder, stalking, drug abuse<br/><br/>I’ve known <i>You</i> was a polarizing novel since it first reached my radar, and I can definitely confirm this is not a book for everyone. <i>You</i> is filled with characters ranging from flawed to downright disturbed. Throughout the story, it’s easy to feel compelled to sympathize with these characters until you have to remind yourself of </span>
  <span id="freeText9684533666417810562" style="display:none">Wow, this read was a trip! It’s been a hot minute since I’ve read something so psychologically twisted but I am ever so pleased.<br /><br />CW: violence, murder, stalking, drug abuse<br /><br />I’ve known <i>You</i> was a polarizing novel since it first reached my radar, and I can definitely confirm this is not a book for everyone. <i>You</i> is filled with characters ranging from flawed to downright disturbed. Throughout the story, it’s easy to feel compelled to sympathize with these characters until you have to remind yourself of all the shitty things they do to stop yourself. It is immensely though-provoking while remaining entertaining. It was a book I truly could not get myself to put down.<br /><br />I think the choice of second-person narration was PERFECT for this story. Second-person can be difficult to successfully execute, but Caroline Kepnes is such a talented writer. Especially listening to the audiobook and having someone TELL ME how they are stalking me really added to the story. (The narrator’s cadence was flawless and I would 1000% recommend the audio version.) Kepnes truly captured the mind of a stalker, while also allowing him to remain human, which was an immensely creepy and twisted experience to unpack.<br /><br />My only gripe with this story is I found it predictable all-throughout. Once the dynamic between Joe and Beck was established, it was not difficult to assume every major plot point to occur. The ending was also so painfully obvious. I do recognize the message that comes with it, but I really wish the author had decided to do something unique. <br /><br /><i>You</i> is a novel unlike many others. If you have a penchant for the morbid and taboo parts of our society, this is a story I would absolutely recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9684533666417810562" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2932321644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2932321644" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2932321644?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2932321644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3898726613291269598">They always say the book is always better than its adaptation. Even Kubrick’s Shinning disappointed Stephen King and he told that “the Shining” movie version was like a big, beautiful Cadillac with no engine inside it.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578985407i/28774464._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>It is always risky to see the adaptions because when the screenwriter turned at least 300 paged books into 100 paged screenplay, editing details and changes about the story’s construction may kill the soul and spirit of the original story. As it happened to Bird Box, remake of Pet </span>
  <span id="freeText3898726613291269598" style="display:none">They always say the book is always better than its adaptation. Even Kubrick’s Shinning disappointed Stephen King and he told that “the Shining” movie version was like a big, beautiful Cadillac with no engine inside it.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1578985407i/28774464._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It is always risky to see the adaptions because when the screenwriter turned at least 300 paged books into 100 paged screenplay, editing details and changes about the story’s construction may kill the soul and spirit of the original story. As it happened to Bird Box, remake of Pet Semetary, Under the Dome, Dune, Hunger Games, Dark Tower, The Girl On The Train, Paper Towns, Lovely Bones, My Sister’s Keeper etc. (The list never ends.)<br><br> But as soon as I read “You”, too much dislikable characters’ existence exhausted me. Joe’s weak imitation of American Psycho’s Patrick Bateman, his creepy, disturbing narration purely irritated me. I love dark books but I had so many questions why Joe chose Guinevere because she seemed like so superficial, self-sufficient, untrustworthy, spineless character. Even her BFF evil Peach has more spine than her. She is a villanelle and she doesn’t act like decent person. <br><br> But when I watch Sera Gamble’s TV adaption, I changed my mind about “the book is always better” myth. (Or mostly it’s a fact!!) Because the series are really better than the book. But the dangerous thing is Penn Badgley became the greatest Joe Goldberg you can imagine. He brought passion, loneliness, kindness to the character and with the connection of little Paco, the screenwriter added the humanity that we’ve been longed for when we’re reading the book. But the dangerous part is we like so much and we root for Joe! So we start to turn into fans of a sociopath killer. Damn! What have you done Penn Badgley?<br><br> And TV version of Guinevere turned into a more likable, profound character who is struggling writer.<br>I think as a book, lack of emotions, profoundness, empathy of the characters and sociopath POV, nerve-bending, stalker narration made me lose my interest for this book. I don’t know I could read the sequel. I think choosing the second season of the adaption by skipping the book might be better option for me!<br><br><a href="https://niluferozmekik.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/nilylovestoread/" rel="nofollow noopener">instagram</a><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/nilufer.ozmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a><br><a href="https://twitter.com/NiluferOzmekik" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3898726613291269598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2221697259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2221697259" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2221697259?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476785608" href="/book/show/23492630-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=non-ya">non-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=favorites-2017">favorites-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=4-and-a-half-stars">4-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=recommend">recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=mystery-thriller-horror-etc">mystery-thriller-horror-etc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2221697259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17900980054334680316">reread this book just armed with the knowledge that I can picture Joe Goldberg as Penn Badgley<br/><br/>(lowered to a 4.5 upon reread)<br/><br/>------------<br/><br/>On the last day of 2017, here's the full review of my last favorite of the year.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/01/04/you-review-the-last-and-practically-only-favorite-read-of-2017/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>I only know one way to like music. That is when you hear a song and you’re instantly like, <i>Holy shit this is THE SONG</i>, and then you are fully unable to listen to any other music, everything else pales in comparison, you can only listen to this </span>
  <span id="freeText17900980054334680316" style="display:none">reread this book just armed with the knowledge that I can picture Joe Goldberg as Penn Badgley<br /><br />(lowered to a 4.5 upon reread)<br /><br />------------<br /><br />On the last day of 2017, here's the full review of my last favorite of the year.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/01/04/you-review-the-last-and-practically-only-favorite-read-of-2017/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />I only know one way to like music. That is when you hear a song and you’re instantly like, <i>Holy shit this is THE SONG</i>, and then you are fully unable to listen to any other music, everything else pales in comparison, you can only listen to this one song on an endless loop until you’re eventually so sick of it that you can’t even listen to it for approximately twelve calendar months.<br /><br />I’m currently in this cycle with the song “You,” by the 1975. (Which, as a side-note, is a band I refuse to listen to purposefully because I find it really pretentious and I think their fans are super like, <i>Oh, you like a song by the 1975? That’s cute. I knew about them before their EP released. Yeah I picked up a conch shell that washed up on the shores of northern England and I listened to it and out from it emerged the dulcet tones of pre-label signing the 1975.</i>)<br /><br />It’s really inconvenient to use “the 1975” in a sentence. Inconsiderate band-naming: add it to the list of why I’ll never be an intentional fan of theirs.<br /><br />Anyway.<br /><br />All of that is to say that the same-named song to this book added to the already-heady experience of reading this book.<br /><br />And boy was it heady.<br /><br />I am really hard on all books. My average rating for 2017 was 2.7, which is truly dismal. I’m aware of that. I’m probably cynical and bitter and I’m definitely critical, it’s true. But it’s all especially true when it comes to thrillers.<br /><br />I only like thrillers if they scare me. And, as someone who is scared of heights and things jumping out at me and walking at night and murderers and mice and robberies and bugs touching me and germs and the alarm system in my apartment that randomly, arbitrarily speaks in a robotic woman’s voice, it doesn’t seem like that’d be a high bar to reach.<br /><br />But books rarely scare me! And the amazing, fabulous, world-changing and life-redefining news is this book creeped the sh*t out of me.<br /><br />Caroline Kepnes is a genius. She figured out something basic and elemental and applicable: People are the most scared when they think that a scary thing - even if it’s not the scariest possible thing - could happen to them.<br /><br />And what happened in <i>You</i> is creepy and sometimes disgusting and visceral and awful...and so, so, so, so possible.<br /><br />We follow Joe. Joe is a man in his mid-to-late twenties who works in a bookstore. He loves to read; he’s kind of technologically disengaged; he’s a bit pretentious and New York born-and-bred; he’s a high school dropout but pretty consistently the smartest guy in the room.<br /><br />Kind of a dream guy on paper, if I’m being totally honest.<br /><br />One day, a woman walks into the bookstore - she’s exactly Joe’s Natalie Portman-esque type. They flirt at the register. It’s a totally normal interaction.<br /><br />Except then Joe looks at the name on the credit card. And he Googles. And he stalks Twitter, and Facebook, and Google Maps, and he knows her address and her friends and her plans and where she’ll be and who she is and where she went to college and her job and he can read her writing and he has access to hundreds of pictures and her favorite movie and the books she loves. <br /><br />Even easier because this girl, Beck, always has her windows open in her safe neighborhood full of the unsuspicious rich.<br /><br />So Joe pursues Beck. It’s just a little simpler, because he can read her emails and visit her therapist and buy club soda from her druggie old-money lover.<br /><br />This book is, in other words, a nightmare.<br /><br />I’d imagine it’s really polarizing. This book exposes a lot about what might shame us. It’s hard to admit that sometimes you catch yourself rooting for Joe. It’s even harder to admit what you’d do if you were Beck. Because for me: I’d flirt with the guy at the bookstore register. I’d be pleasantly surprised to see him coincidentally later. I’d be flattered by the extent to which he’s into me. It’s really doubtful that I’d ever suspect him of hoarding my old phone or stealing my high school yearbook.<br /><br />Which is to say: I’d fall for Joe, and his traps.<br /><br />And what could be scarier than that?<br /><br />Bottom line: One of the best thrillers. Period.<br /><br />Happy new year, gang.<br /><br />---<br />PRE-REVIEW<br /><br />(changing my rating to five stars for the moment; still subject to change because I am one indecisive b*tch)<br /><br />---<br /><br />YOOOOOOOOO.<br /><br />HAHAHAHA DUDE WHAT?!?!?!?!?!?!<br /><br />review to come when my thoughts come in actual phrases</span>
  <a data-text-id="17900980054334680316" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476785592" href="/book/show/20821614-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1149794312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4485465157103551301">I don't even want to know what kind of research needed to be done to write this novel. The ending left a pretty big plot berg, but YOU was strangely addictive. What's even more strange was how Kepnes somehow got me to both root for Joe and be disgusted with him and myself simultaneously. Excuse me, I need to shower. </span>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dark-themes">dark-themes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=kidnapped">kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=hate-that-i-love-them">hate-that-i-love-them</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1359335747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7404200012805109834">Brilliant! This book was unlike anything I've ever read before. I enjoyed every minute of this deranged story.<br/><br/>Welcome to the mind of Joe, a seemingly normal guy that works in a bookshop. However, there is nothing normal about Joe. His mind is a fascinating place to be, turning brief encounters into meaningful events and even, obsessions. He's a stalker, a murderer and the most candidly honest character that I've ever crossed.<br/><br/>The thing about Joe is that his craziness sucks you in. I loved Joe and</span>
  <span id="freeText7404200012805109834" style="display:none">Brilliant! This book was unlike anything I've ever read before. I enjoyed every minute of this deranged story.<br /><br />Welcome to the mind of Joe, a seemingly normal guy that works in a bookshop. However, there is nothing normal about Joe. His mind is a fascinating place to be, turning brief encounters into meaningful events and even, obsessions. He's a stalker, a murderer and the most candidly honest character that I've ever crossed.<br /><br />The thing about Joe is that his craziness sucks you in. I loved Joe and all of his totally inappropriate behaviors. I found myself laughing my ass off at his brutally honest inner monologues on people and society in general. I kept thinking, "Am I supposed to be laughing so much?" <br /><br />As Joe fixates on Beck, he finds ways to infiltrate her life. He stalks her, invades her most private moments and thoughts. He even eliminates those that would bring her down. <br /><br />There's no denying that he's bat-shit crazy. However, I still loved him. I never thought I'd be able to connect with a character like Joe, but I couldn't get enough of him. <br /><br />I listened to the Audible version and it was phenomenal! The narrator did a superb job. I'm not sure I would've loved it as much if I had read the kindle version. He really brought a lot to the story.<br /><br />It did take me a little time to get into this book. Joe was unlike any character I'd ever encountered and his inner rants took some getting used to. He grew on me quickly though, becoming a favorite character of mine in no time.<br /><br />If you're looking for something suspenseful, creepy, mysterious and a little quirky, look no further! This is a great read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7404200012805109834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1097376146" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097376146" />
    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1097376146?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476785592" href="/book/show/20821614-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097376146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5898443800836706392">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Re-read October 2020: If you know me you know I'm not typically one to do a re-read. Buuuuuuuuuut when I was lucky enough to have my "wish" granted over on NetGalley for the latest Joe and was about 20 pages into it I decided I wanted to experience all of the crazy again. The only thing I have to say for this new review:<br/><br/><a href='https://lunapic.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603117061ra/30258605.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓<br/><br/><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW:</b><br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416596813ra/12013557.gif' alt='Commercial Photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Before I even get started, let me say this is not a book for everyo</span>
  <span id="freeText5898443800836706392" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Re-read October 2020: If you know me you know I'm not typically one to do a re-read. Buuuuuuuuuut when I was lucky enough to have my "wish" granted over on NetGalley for the latest Joe and was about 20 pages into it I decided I wanted to experience all of the crazy again. The only thing I have to say for this new review:<br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603117061ra/30258605.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓↓<br><br><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW:</b><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416596813ra/12013557.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Before I even get started, let me say this is not a book for everyone. Hell, it might not be a book for anyone except for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1093750289?book_show_action=false&amp;page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Snotchocheez</a> and myself. There is no middle-ground to be had here. This book is offensive and the characters are all vile and I expect opinions to be extremely polarized. And I totally respect that . . . but please have the decency to not troll my review and tell me how wrong I am or that I’m a pscyho. I’m already aware of those facts. Now on with the show . . .<br><br>You walk in to the bookstore where I work. Rather than picking up the shitty Dan Brown’s and other bestsellers that all the no-brainers are reading, you choose Spalding Gray and Paula Fox. You’re not only attractive – very reminiscent of Natalie Portman – you’re also intelligent. And as we exchange pleasantries while I’m checking you out (your books, that is), you prove to be witty as well. <b>
  <i>“If we were teenagers, I could kiss you. But I’m on a platform behind a counter wearing a name tag and we’re too old to be young. Night moves don’t work in the morning, and the light pours in through the window.”</i>
</b> So you take your bag and go on your way . . . and I take a glance at your credit card receipt before shoving it through the cash drawer. “Guinevere Beck” – an usual name. <b>
  <i>“You are Charlotte’s Web and I could love you.” “The internet was designed with love in mind. It gave me so much of you . . .”</i>
</b><br><br>So there you have it. Joe is a stalker - a textbook example of the scariest version of one at that. He sets his sights on Beck and is willing to do anything to make her his. And I <i>really</i> loved him. No, not in the “boy do I wish I had some fucked up weirdo in my life who would break into my house and sniff my underpants” (I've been married to <b>that</b> guy for a long time now *rimshot*) kind of love him, but I couldn’t stop reading his story. Caroline Kepnes managed not only to write the most revolting character I’ve ever loved (move over, Herman Koch, you ain’t got nothin’ on this gal), but on top of it all she wrote the book from Joe's perspective. I <b>hate</b> that . . . but I loved this book. <br><br>Kepnes even managed to make me forget Joe was a total psycho on occasion. At times he was so relatable, and his opinions were spot-on . . . like when he and Beck went on an IKEA shopping spree together:<br><br><b>
  <i>“Life at IKEA is not like life at IKEA in the movies. It’s a dystopian nightmare come true where all furniture is cut from the same hunk of cheap-ass wood, where all rooms were furnished with items that came out of the exact same factory at the exact same time. It smells like body odor and Febreze and baby shit and farts and meatballs and nail polish and more baby shit – doesn’t anyone get a babysitter anymore? – and it is loud.”</i>
</b><br><br>Joe is the only man I know who not only willingly references <i>500 Days of Summer</i>, but dreams he could have a magical IKEA moment like JGL and Zoey Deschanel had in that movie . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416596813ra/12013558.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Through all the crazy (and let me tell you there is <b>A LOT</b> of crazy), I held out hope for Joe – just like he held out hope for himself.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Happiness is believing that you’re gonna be happy. It’s hope.”</i>
</b><br><br>And for a bit it looked like things might work out (after all – Beck was no prize in the normal department herself).<br><br><b>
  <i>“We are a dream couple, we are what happens after Meg Ryan and Tom Hanks finally kiss, after cancer-free Joe Gordon-Levitt and sweet shrink-in-training Anna Kendrick eat their pizza in 50/50. We are Winona Ryder and Ethan Hawke after U2 finishes singing 'All I Want Is You'.”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416596813ra/12013559.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But then Beck discovers his secret . . . in the form of a used tampon he saved - along with other not-so-normal keepsakes - and I realized there was never going to be a normal. And that I’m probably going to be considered certifiable for even admitting I enjoyed this book – let alone wishing for some kind of happy ending. I admit it. I’m nuts. This book made me crazy. It turned wrong into right and bad into good and I couldn’t stop reading it. I was mesmerized. It gets 5 Stars and it’s easily going down as one of the Top 10 books I read in 2014.<br><br>All I can think now is that it’s weird enough to admit to loving a story like this, but to be Caroline Kepnes and actually have this thing COME OUT OF YOUR BRAIN???? Oh, she has to be the most delicious weirdo I’d ever care to meet. Her writing is brilliant and I can’t wait to see what she comes up with next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5898443800836706392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_983351385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/983351385" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/983351385?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476785592" href="/book/show/20821614-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=jury-duty-book">jury-duty-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer983351385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16532912230241832430"><i>…the problem with books is that they end. They seduce you. They spread their legs to you and pull you inside. And you go deep and leave your possessions and your ties to the world at the door and you like it inside and you don't want for your possessions or your ties and then, the book evaporates.</i><br/><br/>this was recommended to me by eeeeeveryone a few years back when it seemed a little cult was being formed around this book, and i'd been meaning to read it for a long time; so long, in fact, that i'd fo</span>
  <span id="freeText16532912230241832430" style="display:none"><i>…the problem with books is that they end. They seduce you. They spread their legs to you and pull you inside. And you go deep and leave your possessions and your ties to the world at the door and you like it inside and you don't want for your possessions or your ties and then, the book evaporates.</i><br><br>this was recommended to me by eeeeeveryone a few years back when it seemed a little cult was being formed around this book, and i'd been meaning to read it for a long time; so long, in fact, that i'd forgotten i had already bought a digital copy on my NOOK and then much later went out and bought a paperback copy like a fool. and when i found myself conscripted for jury duty and in need of something that was going to be entertaining enough to block out the noise of the game shows they play so loudly in the jury duty waiting room (WHY DO YOU DO THIS, JURY DUTY, WHYYYY??), i figured this would be a good choice, and i could finally see what all the fuss was about.<br><br>and it absolutely delivered what i needed - family feud did not stand a chance against this extremely immersive tale of obsession and crime and unpleasant people colliding. <br><br>however, all of you people who told me i was going to "fall in love with joe," you have officially lost all rights to set me up on blind dates should i ever require that sort of service. and if you yourself fell in love with him, i think i should stage an intervention on you. because while he is certainly … <i>devoted</i> to the object of his desire, he's pretty shitty boyfriend material. yes, i appreciate that he's a bookperson, and there's appeal to someone whose declarations of love are so in line with my own interests:<br><br><i>I want to bring you all the books in the world…</i><br><br>and i appreciate some of his observations and attitudes, but all the window-peeping and social media violations and kidnapping and murder and desperate neediness tied to email and text response-time - those are less attractive qualities when i'm looking for a mate. <br><br>although he's not wrong about some things, and we could probably be friends, if not lovers:<br><br>-<i>Work in a bookstore and learn that most people in this world feel guilty about being who they are.</i><br><br>-<i>If people could handle their self-loathing, customer service would be smoother.</i><br><br>-<i>Life at IKEA is not like life at IKEA in the movies.</i><br><br>-<i>What's the only thing more sexless than lunch? Brunch, a meal invented by rich white chicks to rationalize day drinking and bingeing on French toast.</i><br><br>although i had to HHMPH at his comment about rhode island:<br><br><i>(nowhere is far from anywhere in a state this small)</i><br><br>i also really like the fact that he has no illusions about beck; he acknowledges her many flaws and his 'love' for her is clear-eyed without any pedestal idealization:<br><br>-<i>You tweet more often than you write and this could be why you're getting your MFA from the New School and not from Columbia.</i><br><br>-<i>…I know you so well, Beck. You are charisma, you are sick, and for some reason you are a magnet for weak, spineless people...</i><br><br>the best thing about this book is its breezy tone. it's not an intense nailbiting horror story of an innocent woman victimized by a deluded stalker who believes they are cosmically meant to be. beck is such a shitty person, you never really see her as a victim, and since this is told in second person, through joe's perspective, it's easy to sympathize with him despite his many transgressions. even in its darkest scenes, it's a funny book, very reminiscent of bret easton ellis, who is winkingly referenced within the text along with many many other books; another reason this is so popular with all the booknerds. we do love our own kind.<br><br>apart from the humor and the booksnark, i enjoyed kepnes' treatment of social class and stratification. i know, zzzzzzz, right? and it's only a minor point, but i was struck by beck's sort of trickle-down slummery; she's from nantucket, known for inspiring rude limericks and, like most island or coastal locales in new england, home to a wildly uneven distribution of wealth between its townie and tourist populations. beck is one of the former:<br><br><i>You hail from farmers and you're fond of saying that you don't have "a place" on Nantucket, but that your family made a <b>home</b> there.</i><br><br>and yet her friendships and relationships are with those far wealthier; toxic people like peach and benji, who embody the "careless people" that populate <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4671.The_Great_Gatsby" title="The Great Gatsby by F. Scott Fitzgerald" rel="nofollow noopener">The Great Gatsby</a>: <br><br><i>You are the townie and Benji is the tourist who literally enters you and uses you as a vacation from the wear and tear of the artisanal club soda business only to dump you before Labor Day… Your emotional livelihood is a demented seasonal economy where Labor Day is every other fucking day.</i><br><br>and<br><br><i>He rents you out, the same way he rents loft space on SoBro (South Bronx to those of us who don't need to make up bullshit pet names for neighborhoods where we're not wanted.)</i><br><br>but with joe, the solidly middle-class beck is the one dating down - with a bookstore clerk from bed-stuy sneered at by peach for his humble background:<br><br><i>"I read that people are starting to move there," she says. "I hope gentrification doesn't destroy all the local color."</i><br><br>wealth isn't a major preoccupation in the book, but it surfaces in interesting ways, particularly for those of us all-too-familiar with the careless values of the easily-monied young new arrivals to these fine boroughs, foisting their pickleback shots and novelty club sodas upon us and steadily driving up our rents. and joe's… interactions with them are wholly satisfying and another reason to applaud this antihero.<br><br>it's a really fun book. i don't think i loved it <i>quite</i> as much as the rabid joe cultists, but it was very engrossing, darkly funny, surprising, and truly entertaining.<br><br>it was also much more erotic than i'd been anticipating, which became a bit awkward when i realized the woman sitting next to me in our jury duty limbo was totally reading along with me during one of these saucy parts and i wanted to shout "IT'S NOT PORN!! IT'S JUST THIS ONE PART!!! JUST WATCH THE FAMILY FEUD, YA PERV!" <br><br>i'm looking forward to reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23492288.Hidden_Bodies__You___2_" title="Hidden Bodies (You, #2) by Caroline Kepnes" rel="nofollow noopener">Hidden Bodies</a>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16532912230241832430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085341826?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781476785592" href="/book/show/20821614-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085341826" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6590580197127990338"><i>Full review posted</i><br/><br/><b>*4 stars for plot--5 stars for writing*</b><br/><br/>It’s been 16 minutes and 4 hours since I’ve finished reading this lunatic of a book—and although I am scared and disturbed and feeling straight-up <i>icky</i>, I’m also outrageously impressed.<br/><br/>With the exception of certain scenarios appearing just a bit <i>too</i> fitting and orchestrated (e.g. multiple persons failing to put pass codes on their phones so a certain stalker can do his job with ease), I think this book was pretty damn amazing. <br/><br/>For me, it w</span>
  <span id="freeText6590580197127990338" style="display:none"><i>Full review posted</i><br /><br /><b>*4 stars for plot--5 stars for writing*</b><br /><br />It’s been 16 minutes and 4 hours since I’ve finished reading this lunatic of a book—and although I am scared and disturbed and feeling straight-up <i>icky</i>, I’m also outrageously impressed.<br /><br />With the exception of certain scenarios appearing just a bit <i>too</i> fitting and orchestrated (e.g. multiple persons failing to put pass codes on their phones so a certain stalker can do his job with ease), I think this book was pretty damn amazing. <br /><br />For me, it was the writing. This author has captured the nature of a stalker (from what I can only assume, since I am not one), <b>brilliantly</b>.<br /><br />We are wedged straight inside the head of <b>Joe</b>, whose internal dialogue aims to make your skin crawl and eyes widen in disbelief. And yet…he can be slightly charming at times, and his psychotic thoughts—although choppy and drenched in delusion—are often hilarious. <br /><br />However, make no mistake—this is not a romance novel. And Joe is <i>not</i> sexy, at least not for me. But he is so real and convincing and <b>constant</b>. His character continues to sink in a downward spiral until there is nothing more left to pity. His issues are not glamorized, and neither are the deep-rooted flaws of the rest of the cast. <br /><br />This story isn't one I’d revisit in the future, although I am glad to have read it. It left me in a sort of dark mood for hours after reading, but emotional side effects are the marks of a job well done. Would definitely recommend to readers who are in it for thrills, not frills! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6590580197127990338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2538037776" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2538037776" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2538037776?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

  <i>“pyscholoonnutjobfreakassholesickocreep...depraved, twisted pantyhoarding creep.” </i>

<div id="review_1127283221" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1127283221" />
    <a title="Edward Lorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn"><img alt="Edward Lorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492199506p2/8850418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1127283221?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Lorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Lorn" href="/user/show/8850418-edward-lorn">Edward Lorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22073005-you">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1127283221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7281517261139765707">First and foremost: THIS IS NOT A ROMANCE. This book is to romance what The Shining is to self-help books.<br/><br/>The titular You is Guinevere Beck (aka Beck, or simply B.), and our narrator is the uber disturbed Joe Goldberg. These two are fucked up beyond all repair and damn fun to read about. If you're a bit demented, that is. Me? I love reading about broken, warped, or all around shit human beings. They don't need to redeem themselves for me to enjoy their stories, but I must understand them. I unde</span>
  <span id="freeText7281517261139765707" style="display:none">First and foremost: THIS IS NOT A ROMANCE. This book is to romance what The Shining is to self-help books.<br /><br />The titular You is Guinevere Beck (aka Beck, or simply B.), and our narrator is the uber disturbed Joe Goldberg. These two are fucked up beyond all repair and damn fun to read about. If you're a bit demented, that is. Me? I love reading about broken, warped, or all around shit human beings. They don't need to redeem themselves for me to enjoy their stories, but I must understand them. I understood Joe and Beck's motivations. And, funnily enough, I liked both of them for different reasons at different times. Kepnes did for me what Gillian Flynn has yet to do: made me care about irredeemable characters. There's no forgiving Joe and Beck (mostly Joe... yup, mostly him), but they're engaging and eerily lovable. I hated myself for feeling bad for these two shits and wanting both of them to come out unscathed. I couldn't help it. This is damn, damn, damndamndamn good writing, folks. <br /><br />YOU has its predictable moments, but that doesn't lessen the impact. The ending is quite powerful, and will probably make it into my top ten endings of all time. Tears were shed. Feels were thunder-kicked into oblivion. This book got to me.<br /><br />Finally, I don't give a flying fuck on hot asphalt what other reviewers say about the pop culture references. They work here. They work to give you a sense of character and place. Yes, pop culture prematurely dates many a work of fiction, but it also helps to cement a feel for the time in which the book was written. Get over it.<br /><br />In summation: If you're a fan of characters who no amount of therapy can cure, you need to read this book. You is being compared to Gone Girl, but in my opinion, Kepnes is a far better writer than Flynn. Flynn might give you characters you can hate. But Kepnes will make you fall in love, and then hate yourself for falling. Highest possible recommendation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7281517261139765707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
